text:
For a great southern taste - grate very cold butter into the dry mixture and gently blend together.  (This keeps the flour light and makes biscuits stay flaky) No need to knead, just carefully press to about 3/4" and cut, simply add enough flour to remove stickiness and definitely use butter instead of shortening.  I have never had such a good biscuit!

text:
This recipe fails to note the two most important things to remember when making biscuits:  (1) ALWAYS use COLD butter/margarine/shortening; that makes for a flaky biscuit. And (2)NEVER NEVER NEVER twist the cutter when you're cutting out the biscuits.  Twisting prevents them from rising.

text:
EXCELLENT recipe!First time I ever made biscuits that weren't as heavy as rocks. My husband grew up on home made biscuits and thought they were as good as any he had ever eaten.  Made 2 batches, one with milk and one with buttermilk, both turned out pretty much the same, we just prefer them made with buttermilk.
Also, I make 4 batches at a time as they freeze really well.  Just be sure to roll them in flour and lay on a tray flat in the freezer.  When they have frozen I put them in a zipperer bags and store in freezer.

text:
Had these biscuits tonight with friends. I made 2 batches and the first one didn't rise hardly at all and suspected my baking powder was the problem so I added an extra heaping teaspoon of fresh baking powder in the 2nd batch that I already had assembled and waiting for the milk. The 2nd batch rose a lot more than the first so I feel that the next time when I use the full tablespoon of fresh BP the biscuits will rise even better. I wonder if this could be the main problem with other reviewers that didn't have good lift in their biscuits. My BP was in what I thought was a very tightly closed container and didn't even think it wouldn't work. Live and learn! UPDATE 12/25. Made 3 double batches this morning. I made them per the recipe and found that 3/4" thick on the bread board made a nicer looking biscuit than patting out to 1/2". My dough was quite moist and used a spatula to get it on to the WELL floured board. Put a bit of flour on my hands and a bit on the top of the dough and just patted it out about half way to what I wanted and then flipped it over onto more flour and patted to thickness I liked. Used a 3 1/2" cutter and got about 11 nice biscuits. Don't twist the cutter when you press it down. I did once just to see if it did make a difference, and yes it did, it sealed the edge and didn't let the biscuit rise hardly at all. Also clean the cutter in between batches. The hardening dough will "crimp" the edge like twisting the cutter. All in all a great, simple recipe!

Got a craving for biscuits 30 minutes ago.  Found this recipe.  Here I sit now, in pools of melty butter.  YUM!  I did use lard instead of shortening.  Barely handled the dough at all.  IMPORTANT FOR NEW BISCUIT BAKERS:  when using a glass or cookie cutter DON'T TWIST IT for any reason. Best biscuits I have ever made.  Thank you!!!

text:
This is my "go to" biscuit recipe. They always turn out. I've gotten creative with the recipe. When I make them I make a double batch, 1/3 I cook as normal biscuits, 1/3 I roll into little balls and roll into butter, cinnamon, and sugar and stack 3 balls to one hole of a muffin tin for sweet monkey bread, and the other 1/3 I roll into little balls and dip in butter, garlic, parmesan, and herbs and place three to a muffin tin hole for monkey bread. They are great as a side to pasta, soup, breakfast, or with jelly. I've also replaced the milk with yogurt and they turn out even more moist. Love them!

To those who are coming out with dense biscuits that don't rise, you are kneading them too much. Mix the milk in just barely enough to moisten the whole mixture and only knead a few times. Your biscuits will come out light and fluffy every time.

text:
These are the flakiest biscuits I have ever made.  I used a stick of cold butter and shredded it in like Julie W suggested and it is delicious!  To make these brown better on top, I run my fingers under the tap and lightly pat a little water on them right before I put them in the oven.  I also make these in double batches to freeze.  Take out what you need and bake right away, increase baking time or thaw on the counter or over night in the fridge.  I "square" cut these out with a pastry blade and the recipe makes 12- 2"x2"x1/2" biscuits.

text:
This recipe is the closest to my Mom's baking powder biscuits I have ever tried to make. I have never been able to get the dough to rise enough or be flaky enough like my Mom's until this recipe. 
The only change or addition I would like to add is that the biscuits should be placed so close together before baking that the dough is " kissing" the next biscuit. This helps to keep moistness in.
Also, if you need to warm them up and want them to be like they had just come out of the oven: place the biscuits loosely in a paperbag, fold the top down and roll it up tightly. Run the water faucet briefly over the bag of biscuits . The outside should look wet, but not saturated. Heat bag of biscuits in the oven on 300 f for about 20 minutes but check the biscuit's warmth every 10-5 minutes.

text:
This is pretty much the same recipe I've used for 30 years except I simplified it by using self-rising flour instead of the flour, baking powder, and salt. Key to success is how "moist" the dough is after you add the liquid to the flour/shortening. You learn over time not too dry and not too wet, but a little too wet is better. Dry dough requires too much handling & makes tough biscuits. Gently "folding" the liquid & dry together till combined works well for me. Sometimes the dough is so moist I use a floured egg turner to gently scoop it over during kneading it. Also, liked grated cold butter as suggested instead of less healthy shortening. Even tried "I can't believe it's not butter". Turned out great!

text:
Pretty awesome!
I followed some suggestions from others and my biscuits came out oh so yummy.
Instead of shortening, I used real butter. I also added some more baking powder.
My dad's side of the family is from the south. I was taught how to make biscuits, but I couldn't remember the recipe, so this was very helpful.
They don't actually 'measure' but eye things. Instead of milk, use butter milk. Also, don't roll the dough out at all. You form each biscuit using your own hands. Granny used her hands while mixing in the butter. I remember sitting at the table and watching her do that.
Form rough balls and gently flatten out the top. Put some oil (canola, veggie) in a spoon and pour a little over the top of each. I remember aunt Brenda using the bottom of the spoon to spread the oil over the top.
The cooking time and temp. were perfect! What a great recipe. Thanks! It was so very helpful, as well as comments from others.

text:
It's almost right, but not quite. I don't want to be the one the rate this as great according to my own changes, so I give it 2 stars for the "almost". my changes: butter NOT shortening, 2 Tbs of sugar (or splenda), 1 Tsp of salt (it's a must for flavor) and you have to learn the amount of kneading required. Too little and it's too crumbly, Too much and it's dense. I also form them freehand instead of messing with a cutter.

text:
I am the first to admit if it can be burned, I will probably burn it. For years, the thought of making homemade biscuits scared me; too much could go wrong, the butter or shortening won't be cold enough, I might work the dough too long, etc. I finally decided to give this very basic recipe a try and it turned out wonderfully! I used a stick of margarine instead of a half cup of shortening. Just to be on the safe side, I placed the butter, flour mixture and cup of (almond) milk in the freezer for about 30 minutes beforehand but this was just me trying too hard not to fail, perhaps. My Ninja dough mixer attachment blended the margarine into the flour mixture perfectly and very fast. The dough was easy to roll out (make sure to have a floured surface with extra flour on hand for when the dough begins to stick). I just grabbed a 12 oz. plastic tumbler cup, dipped the rim into flour and used it to cut out biscuits, being careful not to twist the cup as I read this can have an effect on how the biscuits rise. The size of my biscuits were of a very decent size, about what you would get at a fast food restaurant with egg and the such on them. I made 8 biscuits from my batch of dough, they baked for 10 minutes and turned out perfectly. I was so happy with my accomplishment that I began texting out pics of my amazing ( not burnt!) creation. My only complaint about these biscuits is that they do not have a strong flavor. I am used to the buttermilk flavor of restaurant or store bought b

text:
Just now tried these out! They were delicious!  I was dubious at first b/c the dough was quite crumbly, more so than I'm use to.  But as a rule I don't handle biscuit dough too much b/c it makes flat hard biscuits.  I used butter flavored shortening and older baking powder (I was snowed in and used what I had).  I shaped the crumbly dough into a mound and then rolled out to just a bit over 1/2 inch, and only folded the dough when I ran out of room to cut biscuits (so I wouldn't over handle the dough).  They rose well and tasted great and they were awesomely flaky!  Yay biscuits!

I'm going to try to make a batch and refrigerate it for the next morning so I can give my teachers a good breakfast! When you're rolling the dough, make sure you don't knead it too, too much. text:
I'm a Southern girl, so biscuits are a known institution! We have tried A LOT of biscuit recipes, searching for that perfect one. This is our go-to, the one we come back to over and over. It is the perfect biscuit - flavorful, flaky and well-risen. We do make a couple of adjustments: we use a stick of chilled butter (that we then grate with our grater) in place of shortening and adjust the salt to 1t instead of 1/2t. Just a personal preference but the biscuit recipe is great as is too!

text:
I gave this recipe only three stars because there were a few instructions that were left out and I did almost everything wrong.  In spite of that it came out ok.  After reading reviews I discovered it was ok to use butter but should have used it very cold.  I had warmed it up slightly so it would mix well.  I chose not to roll to 1/2" but  hand shaped to about 3/4 inch.  The point is not NOT overwork the dough to keep tender.  I also didn't use all the liquid suggested and had to cook them about five minutes longer than directed to get a good golden color.   They would have been a gloppy mess with 3/4 c. milk.  In spite of all that, they rose, tasted good and were tender enough.  They would have been more flaky if I had not softened the butter.

text:
Made a tweaked version of this recipe,  in place  of the shorting, I cut in 1/2c cold salted butter cut into small  pieces and using my hands I bleaded it together until the dough was holding together and there wasn't any flour in the bottom of the bowl.  From there I kneaded the dough on a lightly floured surface and then it went back into the bowl and covered with saran wrap and allowed to rest for approximately 15 minutes,  then I began rolling it out to my preferred thickness,  and using a standard drinking glass, I cut out the biscuits, (repeating with the remaining dough until dough is used up),  once the biscuits are in the pan brush with an egg wash,now comes the difference  instead of baking in a traditional oven I used my power air fryer and round metal cake pans for 12-14 min, if using more than one cake pan you'll have to switch the pans at the halfway point to allow even cooking. 
(They were the best biscuits I have ever made, they were fluffy, flaky, soft, this is based on my husbands response .)

I used this recipe as a quick oh no Im out of Bisquick moment. I of course had expired shortening in my pantry (7days old) so I substituted for 1/2c of butter instead. I always use a tad less salt than is ever required. The first thing my son said after biting into his was these taste like saltines ... but he was okay with that and said they were good. Good basic biscuit recipe overall.

text:
Used this recipe very last minutes for biscuits and gravy! 
I cut my cold butter into tiny squares. Stuck the butter in the freezer on a plate, as well as my kitchen aid mixing bowl. Prepared the dry ingredients. Pulled the items out of the freezer. I used the wisk attachment to cut the butter into the flour mix. Cover the mixer with a towel. Some larger chunks still remained. Add milk until just barely combined and turned it out on to my work surface. Used a glass to roll it out and to cut my biscuits. Worked wonderfully!!!!!

Instead of 1/2 cup shortening,  use 1 cup of cold butter (2 sticks) 
Use 3/4 cup of buttermilk instead of white milk.
Do not twist the cutter. Twisting the cutter prevents them from rising.

If you add 1/2 cup of grated cheddar, you'll be lucky to get one for yourself before they all disappear.

This may be a very old-fashioned recipe.  When I cut the shortening into the flour I found I needed and extra 1Tbs. of shortening.  My mother used to insist I sift the flour BEFORE I measure (which I didn't do).  When you sift the flour you add volume making 2 cups more like 2 1/2 cups.  Sift your flour first! text:
Despite forgetting to add salt, this recipe is very good. I look for texture first as flavor can be fixed more or less easily adding or reducing salt. I replaced the shortening for cold unsalted butter. I must say that they were very fluffy and moist inside. Now, good biscuits are more about the process than anything else IMO. I agree with many others in that there are key things to consider when making biscuits. My key things to keep in mind are the following: Do use VERY cold butter. Do NOT manipulate (knead) the dough too much. The heat of the hands will melt the butter and kneading modifies the gluten leading to the undesired hard biscuit. I prefer to pat the dough into a rectangle and fold it into two creating 3 layers. Then, pat it again into a rectangle 1/2"-3/4" thick. Repeat two more times and no more. When using the remnant, pat it again into a rectangle and don't do the folding step. Just cut the biscuits. Arrange them with edges sticking together and if you wish brush with milk or butter before baking. Keep an eye on them until you obtain your desired golden color. These important considerations should give you a biscuit that is fluffy on the inside with a nice golden crust. If you bake them straight out of the freezer (they freeze well) then bake them up to an average time of 15 minutes or less. EDIT: Made this recipe again with a substitution of leavening agent. I used 4tsp of baking powder and 1/2tsp of cream of tartar. Used same procedure and the result was ex

text:
Man these are good biscuits, I used tips from several commenters to make them better:

1. Butter instead of  shortening (Same measure) The tip  about grating the frozen butter works great also, it's bit messy on the grating hand but....whatever. The butter gets uniformly blended with the flour

2. FRESH Baking powder, they were great with my old baking powder, but fresh?  WOW.

3. Add 1/4 cup white granulated sugar to the recipe.  When I 
 first read that tip, it sounded like too much so every time I made them I slowly worked up to 1/4 cup.  Perfect.

4. Twist vs Press: I use a flowered glass as a biscuit cutter, don't twist press straight down.  I tried both ways (by accident) Truly makes a difference.

5. Dough Thickness:  I make the dough roughly 1" think, I only get 6 biscuits but they look perfect

6. Milk:  I normally use 2% milk, this last time I used half 2% milk and half "Half & Half".  Didn't notice any difference, not worth the expense.

7. This is my own observation - Don't bake them too low in the oven, in my case the bottom browns much sooner than the top and is too crusty. In my electric oven I put them on a foil lined cookie sheet on the  third shelf setting or about 10" from the heating element.

Thanks again to lenihan5 for posting this recipe.

text:
Use a stick of (frozen) butter in place of the shortening for flaky buttery biscuits. I used my food processor to mix the dry ingredients and the butter, then transferred to a bowl to add the milk. Mix only until it comes together for nice fluffy biscuits and don't twist the cutter.

If you're having trouble getting your biscuits to rise try using an extra teaspoon of baking powder.  It doesn't affect the flavor and it works. The first time I made these they were pretty flat. Tonight was second time making them and they turned out so nice my husband told me they were better than his mom's.

text:
These were SO easy to make (fun too) and taste amazing with a healthy dollop of butter on top! Followed the recipe to a T, but one thing to add! When you're cutting them into circles, DON'T TWIST THE CUTTER! This will seal the edges and make it so your biscuits don't rise! Also: cook for exactly ten minutes or more: no less! These are SO yummy, and my family loved them. Great recipe!

I made the recipe as pretty much as directed, using butter instead of shortening.  Adding the full 3/4 cup of milk makes a very wet dough - couldn't use biscuit cutters, so I used my trusty pizza cutter and made squares.  I had to use a lot of extra flour on my board and on top of the biscuits to be able to cut them and transport them to the baking pan.  That said, the biscuits themselves were quite good - higher and fluffier than anything I'd made before.  They had a pleasant taste, but not the complex flavor of butter milk biscuits.  Will make these again.

text:
This is really a 4.5 star recipe. The biscuits I made were fantastic. The only actual change I made was the addition of 1 tbsp sugar (or even 1 tsp.)

 What knocks the rating down for me are some missing details. They are both fairly basic baking tricks but if, like me, you don't bake often you may have either not encountered them or forgotten them. Fortunately I read a number of other Comments. 

#1 use cold shortening. Since it's stored at room temperature I cut mine into 1/2 inch or so pats then throw it in the freezer for about 10 minutes. or you could store it in the fridge. A big part of the shortening's role in this recipe is to evaporate away leaving a flaky, crumbly biscuit. It gets warmer as you work it. If it becomes too lquid it will be absorbed too much into the flour resulting in flatter denser biscuits. Starting with cold shortening gives you a bit of a safety cushion. This is also why you use a pastry mixer or a fork instead of a hand or stand mixer.

#2 don't twist the cutter when you cut the biscuit. Twisting the cutter ends up sealing the sides of the biscuit. Again you want the moisture from the shortening to evaporate away. Sealing the sides leaves no where for the moisture to escape to. The resulting moisture leaves the biscuit denser and much less crumbly. I squish the last bits of my dough into round biscuit shapes and sure enough these ones don't rise well. 

A quick google search will turn up a number of videos. Watching someone make the same basic

4-4-2017  ~There are thin biscuits (roll dough to 1/2 thick) and there are thick, tall biscuits (roll dough to 1 thick).  The taste of these (thin) biscuits was there for sure (I could have eaten the whole darn batch), but with this recipe Ive confirmed I like thick biscuits better, if for no other reasons than for eye appeal and the ability to slice or break these apart into nice thick halves.  (In other words, theres no way youd make a sausage, egg and biscuit breakfast sandwich out of these!) Bottom line?  If you want to try these basic biscuits my suggestion would be to roll out your dough to 1 thickness.

text:
As is usually the case with comments on Allrecipes, we change something in this - but for good reason.  Our daughter is allergic to cows milk. So we use soy milk for this recipe for a dairy free biscuit.  They turn out great!

Definitely do not twist the cutter or they won't rise.  Push down and then pull back up.  If the biscuit sticks in the cutter, flick it onto the pan or gently push it out.  Then flour the cutter and use again.

The biscuits are simple but tasty.  Not a butter bomb or too heavy.  They have a light butteryish taste though there are no butter ingredients, and a slight saltiness.

Our family loves these and they're so easy to make!  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
Easy peasy. Followed the advice of another reviewer and used grated frozen butter in placed of the shortening.  I did this by: first sifting all the dry ingredients together, then lighting mixing the milk in by hand with a plastic spatula, then I used a fine grater and grated in the butter stopping as my arm got tired and blending it in by hand gently until lightly combined.  Being careful to not to over mix.  You really just need to lightly combine all ingredients.  Rolled out the dough on the counter with some extra flour and DID NOT work it cut the biscuits without twisting the cutter (another review tip to help rise).  They turned out light and fluffy.  Perfect for biscuits and gravy or just with some jelly.  This will be my new go to recipe!! Thank you!

text:
Great staple recipe to have in a pinch. I read through the reviews and took the advice of grating cold butter (great hack!)
I didn't have baking powder on hand so I replaced it with baking soda and apple cider vinegar. I, also added some sage and rosemary for a little spice. 
They turned out wonderful for a first time/last minute breakfast addition. Next time I plan to roll the dough a little thicker, the biscuits fluffed up beautifully but are on the thinner side. In addition to that, next time I'll bake for 8 minutes, check and reassess as they turned a little crispy with the full 10 minutes. Overall, easy things to tweak and I'm happy with the end result and even moreso is my partner. Sunday Mornings

text:
This is a great base for any type of biscuits you may want to make. I use this recipe all the time! 20 mins tops and you have fresh biscuits ready to eat. I prefer to use butter when I make this recipe but it turns out just as good with the shortening. I often add different ingredients to this recipe to make it different depending on what we are eating it with. Our favourite would have to be 1 cup sharp cheddar cheese and a couple diced jalapeo peppers. Also very good with 1 cup raisins added, or  3/4 cup sharp cheddar cheese and 1/4 cooked ham, or roasted garlic to your liking. Honestly this is such a good recipe you can almost add a cup of any mix of your choice. I will keep making this recipe for years to come. I already know it by heart that's how much I make it! I would and do recommend this recipe to everyone.

text:
I made these and only altered slightly. I have found that if you mix the flour, baking powder, salt, and use room-temp butter instead of shorting and work it into the dough until you get a grainy meal and THEN stick the butter-incorporated flour mix into the fridge for 1 hour before you add the milk the biscuits come out perfectly and have a nice subtle buttery flavor. I have even used this and I rolled it out in two 9 inch disks for a "Breakfast Pie" recipe and as long as you prebake the crust with pie weights at the same temp but half the time of the biscuit recipe you have a super delicious and homemade biscuit crust for any occasion.

I made these biscuits to accompany a beef stew and they were delicious. The kitchen intimidates me, so I wanted to start with a very basic biscuit and this recipe was it. I read a few of the reviews prior to making the recipe and they provided me with some great hints: make sure your shortening is cold, do not twist your cutter (as it seals the edges and they won't rise as nicely), and...smother them in butter while they are hot. These simple biscuits were a hit with my entire family.

Good, light and flaky biscuits, when made per recipe. The dough is not near as sticky as some other biscuit recipes can be, therefore it can be easily kneaded and worked by hand and with minimal additional flour. Without rolling and cutting biscuits, they tend to flake a bit more on their kneading folds. The real highlight of this recipe though: it makes amazing dumplings for chicken and dumplings.

The only reason I'm giving it 4 stars is because I had to change a couple things with this recipe in order for it to turn out really well.  The first time I made these, they tasted very good but did not rise well.  Second time I just changed the shortening to cold butter, like other posters suggested, and grated it into the recipe. city:

region:

country:
None
text:
Great basic biscuit recipe. I used butter instead of shortening and buttermilk instead of milk. If you dont have buttermilk, simply add 1 tablespoon of vinegar to 1 cup milk and let sit for 5 minutes; Buttermilk in a pinch. I also just throw the dry ingredients into my food processor and pulse to mix then add the butter and pulse some more. Last, add the milk and you guessed it, pulsed until the dough forms. Drop it out onto a floured surface and pat down to 3/4 thick and cut your biscuits out. Dont over bake!! Set your timer for 8 minutes and check them, I like the biscuits to be just barely baked and 8 minutes was perfect for that.

Wow I just made homemade biscuits!  And they're delicious!  I subbed butter for the shortening.  I did not have a designated biscuit cutter or round cookie cutter so I cut my dough with an upside down drinking glass.  Turned out perfect!  Don't make the mistake of rolling them too thin...they just don't look right.  The second time rolling out my dough I was a little more conscious of the thickness and consequently those biscuits look more like...biscuits.

This recipe is so simple and makes the perfect biscuit. I use the exact recipe and once the milk goes in I mix it all together and turn it out onto a floured surface. Sometimes I knead, sometimes not. I pat it down to about 1/2 an inch and use a juice glass to cut them...sometimes turning, sometimes not. Never have I made a bad batch. From start to finish it is done in 20 mins and always right on time for dinner.

text:
These always turn out perfectly and my neighbor told me they are even better than her grandmothers - but I'm not supposed to tell anyone...

I should mention that I use salted butter instead of shortening.  Once the dough is flattened out, I flour, fold and flatten - repeat twice more.  This will give the biscuits the layers that make them light and wonderful.  I used to think of this as over handling and thought it would make the biscuits hard, but not so.

oh - and one more thing.  I don't use a biscuit cutter.  I use a sharp knife to cut each one out.  This keeps the edges of the dough from smooshing down and preventing them from rising.

text:
If you've had trouble with biscuits in the past...look no further. This basic recipe is a no brainer and just as easy and quick as any I've ever done. All of the substitutions will work...particularly the swap out of shortening with butter and too...sour or buttermilk. Some tricks besides folding the dough to layer it, is don't over-handle the dough, and using a sharp cutter that won't crush the dough as you're cutting the biscuit. It allows the dough to expand while 
baking...giving that flaky end result.

I tried these thinking they would be easy and taste great, after seeing the high rating. I'm not sure if it's my taste buds or what, but I didn't like them. They tasted way too strong of baking powder (and I even leveled it off so it was the exact amount). I had a gut instinct to add some lemon juice and sugar as a buttermilk substitute that I briefly saw on another recipe, but never use buttermilk & short on time so decided against it. I will try it in the buttermilk substitute in the future, but unfortunately will not try it with this recipe again.  I made these along with a homemade chocolate syrup recipe that I have been bragging on for a long time to my husband - the chocolate syrup turned out great, but was just not enjoyable because the overpowering baking powder taste in the biscuits.  Very disappointed. :(

This was my first time making biscuits and found this super easy. I didn't have shortening, but my mom told me to use frozen butter and a cheese grater. Well grating frozen butter is not that easy so I just chopped it up into pieces as small as I could then mixed it in with the dry ingredients. I also needed a splash or so more milk then was called for, but that was to be expected. Then instead of rolling out the dough, I just scooped out spoonfulls and put them into muffin pans to bake. Everyone loved them. In the muffin pans it help make the outside crisp and the inside was so light and fluffy. Thanks mom for the frozen butter tip.

These were a super simple recipe and makes a great substitute for my normal biscuit recipe when I'm out of self-rising flour.
